GOLDEN ROAD <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.326,t=0.536,r=0.630,b=0.574), with ID 2fa9f192-aaf7-4cad-9541-2f9ed37b95ca -->

Trade and travel rule the pathways of the Golden Road, known for its shining sands and economic strength. Much of this region consists of sprawling desert, but this doesn‚Äôt mean that the area is sparse in population. Coastlines and rivers are the lifeblood of this region, and caravans brave the heat and dangers of well-trodden routes to trade across northern **Garund**. Some of the Inner Sea‚Äôs oldest nations command this area, and ancient lore and valuable treasures can be found amid its shifting sands and storied cities. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.092,t=0.599,r=0.472,b=0.739), with ID 6bbdd2cc-850a-47f6-b7b6-5db41ede7c82 -->

The largest city in the region is the cosmopolitan **Katapesh**, where mercantilism is overseen by a strange group known as the **Pactmasters**. Much of the trade in Katapesh is in goods that can be freely exchanged throughout the Inner Sea region, but the city does just as much business in avenues normally relegated to the black markets of other societies. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.094,t=0.740,r=0.471,b=0.832), with ID 2158aac5-b1c0-4b7d-9b13-645b9a2819ff -->

Qadira‚Äôs cities might not be as individually large as Katapesh, but the nation‚Äôs economy is perhaps the strongest. It‚Äôs certainly the oldest nation in the region, with support from the long-established Padishah Empire <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.094,t=0.832,r=0.471,b=0.893), with ID b76d3b6f-c57c-4dce-aca5-59891d4aa50f -->

of Kelesh to the east. This, coupled with the church of  
Sarenrae‚Äîperhaps the nation‚Äôs most successful cultural  
export to the rest of the Inner Sea region‚Äîhas secured <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.095,t=0.890,r=0.470,b=0.940), with ID 578b9f0e-9f07-47ec-ad03-712a7eaa806c -->

Qadira‚Äôs status as one of the most important centers of
influence on the Golden Road. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.486,t=0.602,r=0.862,b=0.632), with ID 07b1c5ee-f0a2-419f-8b38-bfdc160c2748 -->

To the west, the five city-states of *Thuvia* tinker with the
lost technology of fallen empires, but they‚Äôre most visited
by those seeking a legendary alchemical concoction called
the **sun orchid elixir**, which grants renewed youth to those
who consume it. This treasured commodity is the keystone
of Thuvia‚Äôs place in the Golden Road. Further west, the
nation of **Rahadoum is** perhaps the weakest mercantile
link, but the fact that this society has eschewed the worship
of gods to place its faith in the industry and talent of
mortals alone gives the nation its own compelling draw. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.486,t=0.633,r=0.863,b=0.785), with ID 99d576b4-1874-433f-9df9-c0d5d94d9cee -->

At the center of the Golden Road lies mighty Osirion, one
of the oldest nations of the Inner Sea. While Osirion was
for a time ruled by Qadira, the legacies and monuments of
its early days still stand tall as an indisputable source of
pride and identity to its people. The influence of Osirion‚Äôs
artisans, philosophers, and spellcasters has spread far and
wide, particularly via the Esoteric Order of the Palatine Eye
and the faith of Nethys, whose not-so-humble beginnings
as a mortal wizard can be traced to the very beginning of
Osirion‚Äôs history during the ancient Age of Destiny. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.487,t=0.786,r=0.862,b=0.939), with ID 389792d3-6b62-43e3-bc25-61c6adcb8806 -->

HIGH SEAS <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.407,t=0.538,r=0.638,b=0.574), with ID e9269be7-3c55-45e1-8353-a23546e7f04e -->

From pirate fleets united under the **Hurricane Queen of the Shackles** to an ancient, subaquatic empire of shape-changing monsters led by the sinister veiled masters, the High Seas of Golarion present dangers both above and below the waves. Yet, they also serve as important trade routes, with merchant ships traveling the waters between powerful nations at opposite ends of continents. Sea captains brave the dangers of the High Seas hoping to partake in the fortunes to be made in trade, linking the ports of the Inner Sea to those on the shores of the **Arcadian Ocean**, from the **Mwangi Expanse** to the **Saga Lands**. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.137,t=0.600,r=0.515,b=0.770), with ID 02d13839-e698-4b88-b2f0-26fb8bb16185 -->

Piracy is one of the greatest dangers facing travelers on the High Seas. The immense volcanic archipelago known as the Shackles serves as a haven for these pirates, with their Hurricane Queen providing just enough structure to keep them from going at each other's throats. A great diversity of monsters and threats populate these islands, and the local pirates know which are safe and which to avoid. North of the Shackles lies **Mediogalti Island**. While its only significant port, **Ilizmagorti**, is a known safe harbor for pirates, it's the presence of the infamous **Red Mantis assassins** who rule the isle that gives this region its greatest infamy. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.137,t=0.770,r=0.514,b=0.941), with ID 7842eab0-9863-4935-855b-ea0e9eaf2343 -->

Other ports present their own complications. The city of  
Promise on the remote isle of Hermea, a few hundred miles  
west of Avistan, rewards well those who can negotiate the  
privilege of trade, but such honors are hard won, for this  
closed society doesn‚Äôt allow just anyone to visit. However,  
new stories from this strange island nation claim that a  
recent tumult might break the tradition of isolation (and  
some say oppression) of this dragon-led nation. Farther to  
the north, the elves of the Mordant Spire are even more  
closed to visitors, and for most sailors, the only thing the  
Mordant Spire offers is an unmistakable landmark for  
navigation, as the twisting spire can be seen for miles. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.529,t=0.602,r=0.905,b=0.785), with ID d1e0a0ad-5a7c-43b1-bf93-4c67615ab06d -->

Of all the regions along the Avistani and Garundi
coastlines, none are more hazardous to travel than the waters
tortured by the **Eye of Abendego**. This immense hurricane
first formed at the onset of the Age of Lost Omens, when
storms wracked all of Golarion in the wake of Aroden‚Äôs
death. This hurricane, however, remained permanently.
Its winds and storm surge have destroyed several nations
and transformed a previously key gulf into a navigational
nightmare. What strange force caused and perpetuates the
Eye of Abendego has, to date, eluded all investigation. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.530,t=0.786,r=0.905,b=0.940), with ID de31ff43-3f67-4e9c-a08a-dc20ae362b92 -->

150 <!-- marginalia, from page 0 (l=0.002,t=0.959,r=0.084,b=0.983), with ID 123340d2-7c68-4a7e-944f-486b360429d0 -->

IMPOSSIBLE LANDS <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.275,t=0.535,r=0.682,b=0.575), with ID 0f7b7cfa-2d6d-4076-96a2-47759b7046fb -->

Magic allows for astounding feats, yet even those who
consider themselves experts in the magical arts pause in
wonder before the spectacles to be found in the Impossible
Lands. What‚Äôs taken for granted in these strange and
eclectic nations would be all but impossible elsewhere. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.091,t=0.600,r=0.473,b=0.678), with ID d47036f1-1d51-40c3-b038-527ad64247a6 -->

Take **Geb** as an example. Here, the living are the minority,
supplanted by undeath. Cruelty, sadism, and violence are
the norm, as one might expect of a land ruled by a violent,
undead dictator. This ghost, for whom the country was
named, has ruled his nation for millennia, although for the
past several centuries, the day-to-day rule of the land fell to
his queen, **Arazni**. Her recent disappearance (many would
instead say ‚Äúescape‚Äù) left the government in disarray until
rumors from the north invigorated the ghost sovereign to
again take active leadership of his benighted realm. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.093,t=0.679,r=0.472,b=0.832), with ID 35291d75-89b9-467b-b6dc-d620974397f7 -->

Geb has opposed its northern neighbor, **Nex**, for the entirety of its existence. Also named after its founder, the nation of Nex is a cosmopolitan realm where magic is mundane. The wizard Nex has been missing for ages, yet in his absence, the **Arclords** have ruled quite effectively. Here, powerful constructs patrol the streets, and the practice of **fleshforging** is an accepted and legitimate industry. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.094,t=0.833,r=0.472,b=0.940), with ID 44ef0345-72f6-432e-b787-1defecb5bd2d -->

Between these two opposed nations lies a stretch of land
known as the Mana Wastes, a blasted and blighted badland
formed by the ancient wars between Nex and Geb. The
very magic of these lands is warped beyond control‚Äîor
in many reaches dead entirely‚Äîand peculiar mutants flop
and prowl through storms of blood in search of prey. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.486,t=0.602,r=0.863,b=0.694), with ID b82a156f-72de-409d-908c-98cc2fbb2163 -->

Only in the duchy of Alkenstar does life approach anything near normal, but even here, the assumptions of the rest of the world are turned on their head. With magic being unpredictable, Alkenstar‚Äôs citizens have turned instead to technology. The nation is home to metallurgists and machinists, and the art of gunsmithing gives them an excellent advantage in this part of the world. Exports of firearms have steadily increased over the years, and Alkenstar is emerging as a significant power of its own. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.486,t=0.694,r=0.862,b=0.831), with ID bf5285ac-f446-40f7-86c8-a7f5109d44b3 -->

Across the eastern waters of the **Obari Ocean** lies the final realm of the Impossible Lands: the island nation of **Jalmeray**. Here, it isn‚Äôt just magic that allows for impossibilities, but also focused training and practices of self-perfection. The people of Jalmeray have accomplished astounding physical feats and achieved remarkable intellectual insights through these long-honed methods. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.487,t=0.832,r=0.861,b=0.939), with ID ce7b5e62-eb9b-41f7-94cf-4076f6ae9cf0 -->

Summary : This is a digital illustration depicting a sunlit ancient ruin complex in a mountainous jungle setting, viewed from a shadowed forest foreground. The image is used as thematic artwork for the "Pathfinder GM Core" book.

illustration:
Scene Overview :
  ‚Ä¢ The main subject is a sprawling, stepped stone ruin complex with pyramid-like structures and large archways, illuminated by sunlight.
  ‚Ä¢ The setting is a lush, mountainous jungle valley, with mist and distant peaks in the background.
  ‚Ä¢ The perspective is from a shaded forested area in the foreground, looking out toward the ruins in the midground and background.
  ‚Ä¢ The composition uses strong contrast between the dark foreground and the brightly lit ruins.
  ‚Ä¢ The color palette is dominated by greens, blues, and yellows, with sunlight highlighting the ruins.

Technical Details :
  ‚Ä¢ No scale bar, magnification, or scientific annotation is present.
  ‚Ä¢ The upper left corner features the "Pathfinder GM Core" logo and a partial illustration of a dragon.
  ‚Ä¢ No on-image UI elements or text (other than the logo) are present.

Spatial Relationships :
  ‚Ä¢ Foreground: Dense foliage, rocks, and tree branches frame the lower and right edges, creating a sense of depth.
  ‚Ä¢ Midground: The ruins are centrally placed, occupying the sunlit valley floor.
  ‚Ä¢ Background: Mountain ridges and misty sky provide a dramatic backdrop.
  ‚Ä¢ Birds are flying above the ruins, adding a sense of scale and movement.

Analysis :
  ‚Ä¢ The illustration conveys a sense of adventure and mystery, emphasizing the grandeur and isolation of the ancient ruins.
  ‚Ä¢ The use of lighting draws the viewer's eye to the ruins, suggesting they are the focal point and possibly a destination for exploration.
  ‚Ä¢ The framing with dark foliage enhances the feeling of discovery, as if the viewer is emerging from the jungle to behold the ruins. <!-- figure, from page 0 (l=0.001,t=0.004,r=0.997,b=0.520), with ID 17155d38-c475-4c72-b51d-a788d037ee50 -->

MWANGI EXPANSE <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.329,t=0.536,r=0.711,b=0.576), with ID 44ef2773-3782-47fb-9fca-931d1429587d -->

The Mwangi Expanse is home to a wide array of
civilizations, both past and present, even as it holds the
largest stretch of wilderness in the Inner Sea region. In fact,
one of the first civilizations to rise from the ashes after
Earthfall did so in this land‚Äîthe nation of Shory and its
flying cities, which spurred many modern schools of magic. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.137,t=0.600,r=0.515,b=0.694), with ID 899a4253-534c-408e-8d1b-4a5edca09046 -->

Some Mwangi cities and kingdoms were lost far more
recently than those ancient wonders. When the **Eye of
Abendego** formed just over a century ago, its winds and
waves flooded two significant realms along Garund‚Äôs west
coast. Where once stood the nations of **Lirgen** and **Yamasa**
now stretch only the **Sodden Lands**, a swath of swampland
and salt marshes held by rival gangs of scavengers and
monsters. Even more recently, the powerful city-state of <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.139,t=0.694,r=0.513,b=0.821), with ID 241dafa6-6fb6-4506-9937-bc64520bdff2 -->

Usaro fell into chaos when its brutal leader, **Ruthazek the Gorilla King**, was slain by adventurers. In only a few short years, the power vacuum has caused significant damage as disparate factions feud among themselves. A long lineage of demonically infused Gorilla Kings has ruled Usaro over the centuries, and so a new one will likely soon rise to seize control of Usaro, but for the moment, this sinister region lacks a head to focus its wrath. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.139,t=0.818,r=0.513,b=0.940), with ID e538b6e1-7af9-42d1-b7d3-6558bfc89153 -->

Despite these instances of ruin, the Mwangi Expanse
hosts a wealth of diverse and powerful city-states within
its reaches. In **Bloodcove**, the ruthless mercantile league
of the **Aspis Consortium** vies against the **Free Captains of
the Shackles** for economic power. Farther south along the
coast stands **Senghor**, whose stance against both piracy
and exploitative trade place the city in stark contrast
to its northern neighbor. The city-state of **Nantambu**
lies far upstream, where its citizens carry on the ancient
traditions of **Old-Mage Jatembe** in combining arcane and
primal magic. Far to the southeast stands **Mzali** under the
oppressive rule of the mummy child-king **Walkena**, though
a group of dissidents called the **Bright Lions** work to resist
his reign. Then, there‚Äôs the trade city of **Kibwe**, where
within its walls dwell an eclectic mix of people who are
overseen by the mysterious and ancient **Pillar-Watchers**. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.530,t=0.603,r=0.905,b=0.846), with ID 273ac6db-f4c6-4d19-8084-4e2674a361c8 -->

Farther south lies the recently freed nation of **Vidrian**. Originally the Chelaxian colony of **Sargava**, Vidrian has now seized its own destiny and cast off its colonial shackles. In so doing, the young nation has exposed itself to the predations of pirates and worse, yet to its citizens, freedom from oppression is well worth that price. <!-- text, from page 0 (l=0.530,t=0.847,r=0.905,b=0.940), with ID f4a529b3-3e23-49f1-a8c3-fc3b8fb7e23b -->
